text:
This was very easy to make and it came out great!  I did make one change, however.  Instead of using all white flour, I used half white flour and half whole wheat flour.  This gave it more fiber and a better, nuttier taste.  Also, I don't use bread flour in my bread machine.  Unbleached all-purpose flour is good enough for me because if I did have all these different flours, I wouldn't have any room in my cabinets.  Although I don't use bread flour, I do add vital wheat gluten, which is available at supermarkets.  This gives more volume to loaves and a more bread-like texture.  The rule is to add one teaspoon of wheat gluten per cup of flour or one and a half teaspoons per cup of whole grain(or whole wheat)flour.  I hope this tip was helpful for those who may be having trouble with the size of their bread loaves as a result of not using bread flour.  I will be making this bread again soon!

I now make this bread all the time - at least twice a week!

text:
WOW!  YUM!  I don't own a bread machine, so I did this:  * Proof one packet of regular yeast with the water and honey for about 8 minutes.   * Add the remaining ingredients all at once and knead in stand mixer with the dough hook for another 8-10 minutes, on a medium/low setting.   * Oil the bowl and the dough, cover it, and let it rise for an hour in a warm oven.   * Punch it down, plop in the loaf pan and rise another 30 minutes.   * Bake at 350 for 30 minutes.    FANTASTIC bread.  Makes a wicket grilled cheese.

text:
I found this to be the best bread machine recipe yet. Not too dense like many are. I, too, increased the yeast and flour. I also have tried several variations that work well and give a different flavor. Try adding seeds or nuts (ie, sunflower, pumpkin, pecans, walnuts). They are delicious. Add them during the second kneed or at the add-in buzzer. Also, you can replace some of the flour (I generally use 1/3-2/3 cup) with either cornmeal or whole wheat flour. I also have replaced the honey with molasses. They all work well and you can mix and match! Enjoy

We love this recipe.

I make this bread 2x per wk. at least.  Family loves it plain, in sandwiches, as french toast etc.

Some small changes that work for me...

Add 1 tbsp brwn sugar, 1/3c whole wheat flour, 1 extra tsp yeast, reduce bread flour to 2c (or 2 1/4c depending on humidity).

Bake on white, med. crust setting for 1.5lb loaf.

Comes out PERFECT every time!

I didn't change any of the ingredients.  I did however use my stand mixer instead of the bread machine.

I proofed the yeast for about 10 minutes in the water (warm), dumped in the rest of the ingredients, let it knead for about 4 minutes, covered and let it rise for 60, punched it down, shaped it into a loaf, and dropped it into a pan.  I covered it and let it rise again for 30 minutes, brushed the top with an egg white, and baked at 350 for about 30 minutes.

This recipe is great, we'll be making it again and again.

text:
These make wonderful rolls.  Use dough setting on machine.  When cycle is done, place dough on lightly flourered surface.  Punch down to remove air.  Shape into 15 round rolls  (knead in slightly more flour if too sticky).    Arrange in 9x12 lightly greased glass pan.  Cover lightly with greased plastic wrap.  Let rise in warm place until doubled (about an hour). Remove plastic.  Bake 375 degrees for 15-18 minutes or until lightly browned.  Turn out onto rack.

text:
To die for! I usually have to tweak bread recipes to get the dough to that smooth, elastic, not too sticky stage. NOT THE CASE with this one. I followed the recipe amounts to the letter, except I was a bit shy on honey so I topped the measuring cup off with a squirt of light corn syrup. I doubled the recipe and made it by hand, no bread machine. I baked at 350 for about twenty minutes, then covered it loosely with foil to avoid a too browned crust and cooked it until it read 190 degrees internally. TO DIE FOR. Slightly sweet, a nice crunchy but not too hard crust and a moist, slightly dense (but in the most pleasant of ways... you know, it has that nice bite and chew to it, it's not all air or spongey) My new go-to Oatmeal bread recipe.

For those who want to know how to make this by hand: I put the warm water in a large bowl, dissolved the yeast on top and let it sit ten minutes. I added the oil, honey, and salt. Mixed gently, added half the flour and mixed on low in my Kitchen Aid (but a wooden spoon is fine) when it was smooth I worked in the rest of the flour and let it mix on with the dough hook about ten minutes. Turned out onto the counter and kneaded by hand for a few minutes. Put in an oiled bowl and rise in a warm place until doubled. Punched down, shaped into a loaf, put in a greased pan and let rise again. Bake at 350 until internal temp reaches 190 degrees. Loosely cover with foil halfway through bake time if you want a softer/lighter crust.

Heavenly.

text:
Loved this recipe.  My incredible picky roommate about died from ecstasy!  I double the recipe for one loaf, adding 3/4 cup honey, 2 1/2 teaspoons yeast, and a little over 5 cups of whole wheat flour to make a whole wheat bread.  I don't have a bread machine, so I dissolved the yeast in 2 cups warm water first before adding the rest of the ingredients and 3 cups flour.  I took the mix out of the bowl and kneaded in the last 2 cups and then continued kneading for 15 minutes.  A great way to make sure of perfect conditions for the bread to rise is to turn on the oven to warm for one minute, then put in the oil covered dough and turn off the oven.  The first time I let the dough rise 1 1/2 hours, second time and hour in the pan.  The second time it rises don't put a cloth over the pan, the dough rises above the pan and a little over the edge (I love that look!) and a cloth will depress it, instead cover with an oiled piece of cling wrap. Great find!

The texture of this bread is light with a slight chew, beautiful. The crust came out kinda dark, as I don't know what all the settings on my machine mean but it did NOT come out as a tough crust. I was surprised and pleased. I didn't have any regular oatmeal so 2 packets of apple cinnamon instant did the trick, although it hardly matters since I see no trace of it in the sliced bread. I suspect this recipe is extremely versatile, you could use any variation of oatmeals from steel cut to instant, dried fruits, nuts, seeds. I might increase the honey next time for a sweeter bread. Can't wait to try this recipe when I finally get a Zojirushi bread machine. This was dang good in my Mr. Coffee breadmaker that I got for $3 at a garage sale.

text:
Too bad we can't do half stars, because I would give this recipe 4 1/2. This is because I did make some changes. I proofed one packet of Hodgson Mill Active Dry Yeast in  1/4 cup water with 1/4 tsp of natural sugar (per instructions) for about 5-10 minutes. I warmed up the remaining 3/4 water to add later to the recipe. I put everything, with the exception of starting out with 1 1/2 flour, in the food processor and mixed thoroughly. Then I added another whole cup of flour gradually and pulsing it til it was mixed. That brings the total flour tally to 2 1/2 cups. I also put 1 tbsp of vital wheat gluten per 1 cup of unbleached flour. Then I kneaded the dough for about 8-10 minutes of a floured surface, adding a little more flour each time it got sticky. Put it in an oiled bowl covered with a damp cloth and stuck it in a warmed oven for 1 hour, then punched dough down and put it in a 9x5x3 loaf pan lined with parchment paper and covered it again and put it in warmed oven for 45 minutes (I would recommend sprinkling a little flour on top before covering it a second time as the dough will stick to the damp cloth). Then took loaf pan with dough out and let it rise another 15 minutes while I warmed up the oven to 350. Baked the loaf at 350 for 35 minutes as recommended by another reviewer. Let it cool on rack for 5-10 minutes then put in into a plastic bread bag so the heat would help keep the loaf soft. Husband and kids gave a big thumbs up!! Thank you!! :)

4-1/2 stars for this. Lovely flavor and moist texture. I did not find it to be a "sweet" bread as some earlier reviews said.  Perfect for sandwiches or toasting, and a good keeper. After 3 days it was better for toasting, just too crumbly for sandwiches, so use it as quickly as possible, or freeze slices for later use. Will keep well frozen for up to one month if wrapped securely (I put two slices in one sandwich sized ziploc bag.)

text:
My family - and everyone else! - LOVES this bread. I make it by hand - whips up in no time. Dump dry ingredients into a bowl, add the honey (or brown sugar) and oil, then I just add a bit of hot water at a time until it makes a nice dough. Oil slightly, cover to rise, then knead for 3 min, shape, bake 350 for 35 min. I also use a partial whole wheat flour we buy in the health food store. It's fantastic bread, super-easy to make, and a real crowd pleaser.

text:
I just made this and it turned out perfectly! I did NOT use a bread machine though. If you do not have a bread machine, then follow these directions:
Pour yeast into a bowl. In a glass measuring cup, combine hot water and honey, stir.  Pour water/honey mixture on top of yeast and let it stand 5-10 minutes. Combine remaining ingredients in a separate bowl. Combine dry ingredients with the risen yeast mixture. Proof dough in a well oiled bowl till it has doubled in size. Once it has doubled in size, punch down and separate into 2 equal size dough balls.  Shape each dough half into rounded loaves  and put in a greased loaf pan. Let dough double in size in the loaf pans. Then bake in the oven @ 350 degrees for 30 minutes. Turned out beautifully delicious!

We love this bread!  I substitute 1 cup whole wheat flour, 1 cup white flour and 1/3 c. oat bran for the white flour. I also add a an additional 1/4 tsp yeast and 1/2 tsp sugar for a fluffier loaf. I use the bread machine and set it to "dough" and then form it into a loaf and put it in a loaf pan. Let rise for another 30 minutes and then bake. Easy and Excellent!  Thanks for sharing!

text:
Tried this recipe for the first time last week when I ran out of bread and decided to save some money and make my own. I am an avid user of honey, especially raw honey for health reasons, and came across this wonderful recipe. It was so easy to put together! I followed a lot of the advice about using melted butter in place of the oil, which I did. I chose to use unsalted Irish butter (Kerrygold), and it made it so moist and extra delicious. I also decided to add some extra oomph to the bread by adding ground flax seed to the flour measurements. That gave it a nice little nutty flavor and I am very happy with the results. I am currently making another loaf since the other one didn't last long at all (and I live alone). I highly recommend this bread to everyone who loves a nice change from everyday white bread. I love this recipe!!!

I'm re-reviewing this recipe.  I still love the texture and flavor of this bread but I don;t care for the hard crust from being baked in the bread machine.  So, I've been setting the bread maker to the dough cycle, removing the dough, breaking it into 9 even pieces and placing the doughballs into a 9x9 pan.  I Let them rise for about an hour or so, brush with butter (or don't) and bake for 10 min at 350.   Soft and fluffy!

text:
This is a wonderful recipe! I modified it a bit though: I used 1 tablespoon of melted butter in place of the vegetable oil; I used sugar free honey (I have diabetics in my family); I used 2 cups of all-purpose flour and 1/3 cup of whole wheat flour; I added 1 tablespoon of Splenda brown sugar substitute; and I used 1 1/2 teaspoons of bread machine yeast. I set my machine to the dough cycle, and after it was finished, I kneaded the bread slightly and divided it into two loaves. I then further divided the dough into two more parts each, and braided each loaf. I let the 2 loaves raise for about another hour. Then I melted 3 tablespoons of butter and 1 tablespoon of sugar free honey and brushed it over the loaves. I sprinkled the loaves with oats and baked at 375 degrees for about 35 minutes. Everyone LOVED this bread, and it was all gone at the end of the meal! My fiance was even eating up all of the oats that fell off the top when we cut the bread! Thank you Merrilee for a great recipe!

country:

text:
Update: 2016. This is STILL our daily bread recipe. I now bake this in the oven instead of the bread machine. I use a 9" Pain De Mie (Pullman) pan. Cover with plastic wrap, let rise till crown almost touches top, put lid on, bake at 350 degrees for 30 minutes. Remove lid, bake 5 more minutes.
Notes:
1.use quick oats. if you use old fashioned you will need to increase the flour to 2 1/2 cups.
2. I replace a 1/3 of a cup of bread flour with whole wheat. when I replace  2/3 of a cup, I start having issues with rising without adding vital wheat gluten and more yeast.
3. I prefer to use Pillsbury bread flour for a more airy loaf. if I use King Arthur all purpose flour or bread flour I get a very dense loaf. 
4. if I use warm milk or warm water with milk powder I get a softer bread than just using warm water.

Original 2009 review:
 this has become our favorite bread recipe. for our everyday bread i replace a 1/3C b.flour with whole wheat. i bake on 1lb light or else its too dark and too thick crusted. for a supper light and airy bread heat the water to 110, otherwords 80 degrees is just right. our friends ask for this bread!

This recipe was very soupy! I have now made it 3 times and it needs more flour and more yeast. Making it exactly as specifed gives you a non-risen lump. I have added maybe 1/2 cup of flour (didn't measure, just kept adding until I saw a doughy texture like it SHOULD be) and an extra tsp of yeast. Now it has risen and looks great. I have no idea how the 4-5 star people got this to come out right with this recipe!

text:
Wow. Possibly the best bread machine recipe I've ever had. I have a convection bread machine and it tends to make very thick crusts. Anyway, with this recipe it wasn't too bad! I even used the delay cycle and it still turned out perfectly. I also used salted butter instead of oil, and once it was out of the machine I rubbed the crust with some butter to help it soften. I also used a heaping teaspoon of yeast, and 1/4 teaspoon of powdered ginger to a)keep the yeast working and b)help preserve the loaf. That amount of ginger doesn't affect the flavor. So far, it's the only non-totally white bread I can get my DH to eat. Thanks!

text:
The first time I made this bread it puffed up too much so I changed the flour to AP which produced a tighter texture more to my liking.  I noted the dough ball was very wet and sticking to the side of the pan during mixing so I paused the cycle and sprinkled some flour on the dough, about 1 tablespoon, and pushed the dough off the side with a spatula.  Next time I will leave it alone and see what happens.  I set my machine to 1 lb, light crust, basic white setting.  The bread is soft and chewy.  The crust is not too dark, and soft on top.   It makes great toast.

text:
As my Oster machine requires, liquids first. Unlike instructions, I make the yeast go before I add dry ingredients.
water
oil
1 tsp sugar
yeast (prove)
1/4 c honey
1/2 cup old-fashioned rolled oats 
1/2 cup whole oat flour (not stuff with bran removed)
1/8 cup oat bran
2 1/2 cups unbleached all-purpose flour 
1 tsp salt
dash ginger powder 
(I always "ginger it up" when baking with honey)

Fresh out of the machine, now nibbling on my second slice before bed!

Made this in my new Zojirushi Virtuoso Plus. I used half unbleached bread flour, half white whole wheat, and honey in place of molasses. Set the crust to light and removed the loaf as soon as it was done, cooled on a rack and lightly covered with a heavy kitchen towel, so that it would cool slowly and not harden the crust. text:
This bread is delicious and I will make it again.  It's light and fluffy, yet has substance when you chew.  I made only two tiny changes--used 1 1/2 teaspoons of yeast, as many suggested.  Used 2 cups of bread flour and 1/3 cup of White Whole Wheat flour, along with 1 teaspoon of Vital Wheat Gluten to lighten up the wheat flour.   Up to now, I've only used the Dough setting on my bread machine, afraid to bake in the machine since my first loaf burned.  This time I used the Sweet Bread setting, as suggested by another reviewer, which helps to keep bread with high amounts of sugar from burning.   Even with a Light Crust setting, I still got slightly burned bottom and sides, so next time I'll cut the baking time short by about 5 minutes.  This bread is worth experimenting until I get it right!

EDIT:  After using the Sweet Bread setting, Light Crust, and cutting 25 minutes from the baking time (problem with my machine), I was so happy with this bread.  I've made it many times.

text:
It was delicious with the changes I made. I don't have a bread machine and made it like other bread dough (proofing the yeast, kneading, etc.). I one and a halved the recipe and only used 3Tbsps of honey, but it was still slightly sweet. I also substituted melted butter for oil. After letting the dough rise for about 45 minutes, I put balls of dough into greased muffin tins, then let these rise about 30 mins and baked them as rolls (it made 1 1/2 dozen, so the regular recipe should make 1 dozen). Perfect accompaniment for soup or any meal. I know it would make great bread for toast or sandwiches. It would be too sweet for me as the recipe is written, though.

text:
Omg!!! I cannot say enough good things about this recipe. It is fabulous! I have made this three times in 10 days. The first time I made it exactly as written and it was pretty darn good. The next time I made a few modifications so the whole family could enjoy it and to up the whole grains. Here are the changes;
*Pure maple syrup instead of honey (1:1 ratio) so the baby could have some. 
*Butter instead of oil (1:1 ratio) because I like the taste of butter more than oil. 
*1/2 cup  and 1/3 cup of whole wheat bread flour. 
*1 and 1/2 cup of unbleached, white, wheat bread flour. 
*and lastly I brushed about a TBLSP of melted butter on the crust right when I took it out of the bread maker. This resulted in the softest crust I have ever had on a bread maker loaf of bread. Seriously!! 
The bread was just as delicious the next day. I don't know about the day after that because it was all gone.

text:
I recently bought a bread maker and have tried numerous recipes.  This is by far the best one I've found yet!!  SO GOOD!!  The only change I made was to add 1-1/2 tsp. of yeast....oh, and make sure to use warm water.  Also, just for my preference, I subbed 1 cup of white flour for whole wheat.  I threw all the ingredients into the bread maker and selected the dough cycle.  Took out, rolled out the air, placed in a baking pan and let rise for 1-1/2 hours.  Baked at 355F til the inside of the loaf reached 190F (approximately 35 minutes).  Amazing!!!!

I liked this bread. It was tasty. It is soft and a little sweet. More of a dinner type bread than for sandwiches, unless looking for a sweeter taste with a sandwich. I did use the basic setting and light crust as suggested. My only change was subbing 1 cup of the bread flour with Gold Medal's white whole wheat flour and right before the baking on the machine started I sprinkled some rolled oats on the top for garnish.

text:
This bread is the best I have tried yet, and I don't plan to look any further!  I use my kitchen aid because I make 2 loaves at a time and it won't fit in my bread machine.  I let the honey, warm water and yeast sit for about 5 min before adding everything else in the mixing bowl.  I use the dough hook and let it go on the lowest setting for 5 min, adding flour as it goes until the dough doesn't stick to the sides.  Then I let it rise for 30min to 1 hour (doubled in size), punch it down, divide into 2 loaf pans and let it rise another 30 min- 1 hour(the size I want my loaf).  I bake it at 350 for 30 min.  Thanks!!

country:
None
text:
I've made using this recipe as a guide. I first made the recipe three different times in a bread machine, varying from exactly to almost exactly as written (higher oat:flour ratio, more honey etc.), and got delicious but extremely dense bread every time. The texture was not at all OK for sandwiches or toast. It became misshapen basically immediately after cooling and cutting it into neat slices was impossible. We still devoured it, but it was ugly enough that I wouldn't serve it to guests!

Today I finally got the loaf to exactly the right texture. I doubled the yeast (2 tsp) and definitely recommend trying that. In the past, I had also used extra honey because I like this as more of a sweet dinner bread than for sandwiches. It tastes good with 1/4 cup, but if you like more of that sweet roll flavor in a loaf, go for about 1/3 cup.

I use the white bread/medium crust setting on my bread machine. Do NOT use the quick cycle, especially without the added yeast. It needs that extra hour!

Then I kneaded it for a couple minutes on the counter.  The first time I made it I doubled the recipe, used only all purpose flour and added about 1/3 cup of ground flax.  This made one loaf and 8 mini loaves.  The results were great!  The bread was dense and moist, the crust wasn't overly crusty, just the way I like it.  After reading one reviewers comments on how she adds wheat gluten to AP flour rather than buy bread flour I tried to find wheat gluten at the grocery store but was unable to.  So the second time I made the bread I did everything the same, maybe I added a bit more flour as I was feeling cocky due to my past success and I wasn't being as careful with the measuring.  Again, the bread turned out wonderful.  My kids and I love it lightly toasted with peanut butter in the morning.   I'm still going to be on the lookout for wheat gluten because I am curious to see what effect it has but honestly, I love the way this bread has turned out using the all purpose flour.  Thanks for the recipe.

We loved this bread!  I changed the servings to 15 and ended up with 2 medium size loaves - just perfect, 1 to keep, 1 to share!  A few little changes: I did decrease the honey to 1/4 cup as other reviewers mentioned that it ended up too sweet, used 2 1/2 cups reg. flour and 1 cup whole wheat flour (next time will decrease the flour - ended up needing to add more water), and increased the yeast to 2 tsp.  Used the dough cycle on my machine, but decreased the rise time by 15 min. as the dough had reached the top of the machine (oops, might rethink increasing the yeast!).  Formed 2 med. loaves and let rise a second time for 20 minutes.  Baked for 30-35 min. at 350 degrees.  I'm sure my husband will be requesting this one again!

text:
Really good flavor, with just a hint of honey so the bread wasn't overly sweet.
The only drawback is you may have to play with the breadmachine settings.  My loaf was underdone using the cook time indicated in the recipe.  I think a medium or even a dark crust would have been perfect (about 10 - 15 minutes longer than light crust).  Also note, the recipe calls for "rolled oats."  I've heard of this before, but have never seen it/looked for it in the grocery store.  I used regular Quaker Oats and the flavor was fine...in fact, I'm not sure what the difference is, if any, between rolled oats and oats used for oatmeal.  I will make this again, but will alter the cook time.

text:
This bread was FABULOUS.  At first I was apprehensive, and thought that
there was a typo in the recipe.  Looking into my bread machine, the dough
was not merely extra moist.  It was a downright wet "batter", as opposed to
a dough.  Yet, I decided to let the bread machine do it's thing, and was I
ever surprised at the results.  The flavor was excellent, but what I was
most impressed with, was the texture.  Although the bread rose nice and
high, the texture was wonderfully chewy and firm textured.  This particular
bread was also excellent, after it was completely cooled.  I just want to
thank you, Merrilee, for submitting that recipe.
Sincerely yours,
Jeff
